The statute details factors considered under the “best interest of the child” standard, which may include the emotional bonds between child and parent, the willingness and ability of each parent to facilitate a positive relationship with the other parent, the child’s educational needs, and any history of abuse or neglect.  \n    - *Relevance for False Allegations*: Courts assess credibility and can look at patterns. If one parent repeatedly makes unsubstantiated claims, it may reflect poorly on that parent’s willingness to foster a healthy co-parenting environment. Under the best interest standard, courts are often wary of awarding greater custody to a parent who attempts to alienate the other parent.  \n  - **“Bad Faith” Conduct under § 571-46(9)** (or the related subsections): While the specific numbering might vary, there are statutory references that allow the court to impose sanctions or modify arrangements if one parent engages in obstructionist behavior or repeatedly makes false allegations. This provision may empower the court to issue orders compelling compliance and potentially hold non-complying parties in contempt. The statute might also allow the court to order make-up visitations, modify custody if a pattern of denial continues, or impose monetary sanctions or attorney’s fees.\n\n**Practical Takeaway**: The HRS provisions set the legal parameters. Demonstrating a pattern of false allegations not only undermines the accuser’s credibility but can open the door for the court to adjust custody or visitation to ensure the child’s best interests—i.e., a stable, conflict-free relationship with both parents—are protected.\n\n---\n\n### Expanded Review of Hawai`i Family Court Rules (HFCR)  \n**Key Procedural Aspects**:  \n- **Motions (HFCR Rule 7 & 7.1)**: These lay out how to properly file and format motions to enforce visitation or to sanction a parent for misconduct. Understanding these rules ensures that any motion challenging false allegations or seeking enforcement is correctly presented to the court.  \n- **Sanctions (HFCR Rule 11)**: Similar to the federal rule, HFCR Rule 11 requires that attorneys and parties ensure claims are factually and legally grounded. A motion that shows the opposing party continually engages in baseless filings might prompt the court to impose sanctions.  \n- **Injunctions or Protective Orders (HFCR Rule 65)**: While often used to address immediate harm, it can be relevant if a parent is using protective orders in bad faith or as a tool to alienate the other parent.  \n- **Discovery Procedures (HFCR)**: Rules on discovery can be leveraged to obtain evidence disproving allegations—such as text messages, emails, medical or school records—demonstrating that claims were unfounded.\n\n**Practical Takeaway**: Procedural compliance is key. Au-Hoy*: While often cited in divorce and custody contexts, it may not be a flagship case on alienation. Still, it might provide insights into how Hawai`i courts weigh credibility, parental cooperation, and the child’s best interests.  \n- Look for cases where the appellate court discusses the appropriate remedies for a parent who repeatedly violates visitation orders. Even if the case does not mention “parental alienation” explicitly, consistent violation or false allegations are forms of alienation and can inform strategic arguments.\n\n**Reviewing Legal Blogs and Hawai`i Bar Journal**:  \n- Attorneys practicing family law in Hawai`i may have authored articles discussing the challenge of dealing with false allegations and parental alienation indirectly. Identifying even a handful of relevant appellate decisions can guide the structure of arguments, showing how Hawai`i courts have reasoned in similar contexts.\n\n---\n\n### Federal Family Law and Guidelines  \n**U.S. Department of State Family Law Resources**:  \n- While focused largely on international aspects (e.g., Hague Convention), these materials confirm that stable parent-child contact is a globally recognized good. Courts might appreciate references to broader principles that underscore the importance of preventing manipulative tactics.  \n- If allegations border on claims related to international custody or fears of abduction, federal guidelines and treaties might come into play.\n\n**Administration for Children & Families (ACF)**:  \n- The ACF’s child welfare guidelines stress the importance of safe, stable, and nurturing relationships.  \n- Even though these guidelines are not binding, they reflect a consensus: children benefit when both capable parents remain involved, absent credible evidence of harm. Constant false allegations run counter to the child’s well-being and may be presented as undermining federal policy aspirations for child welfare.\n\n**Practical Takeaway**: While not controlling authority in a state custody dispute, these federal sources can provide a policy backdrop. They highlight the unacceptability of obstructing a healthy parent-child relationship and the general policy push towards involving both parents unless there’s a serious safety risk.\n\n---\n\n### Parental Alienation Research  \n**Psychological and Social Science Data**:  \n- Studies on parental alienation indicate that children suffer long-term emotional harm when kept from a loving parent due to one parent’s manipulations.  \n- By citing reputable psychological research (e.g., from APA articles or child development specialists), a motion can argue that false allegations harm the child’s emotional stability and developmental needs.\n\n**Connecting to Hawai`i Context**:  \n- Hawai`i’s courts may be receptive to arguments that emphasize the holistic well-being of the child. Stressing that continuous exposure to parental conflict and unsubstantiated allegations can impair trust, create anxiety, and hinder the child’s cultural and familial identity may be persuasive.  \n- Hawaii’s strong family-oriented culture might align with arguments that the extended family (ohana) and cultural traditions value cooperation, not estrangement. Alienation is not just legally problematic; it’s culturally discordant.\n\n**Practical Takeaway**: Integrating social science research with legal arguments can paint a full picture for the judge: not only is the alienating behavior legally sanctionable, it is also detrimental to the child’s emotional and cultural development.\n\n---\n\n### Cultural and Historical Context  \n**Native Hawaiian Law and Cultural Norms**:  \n- Traditional Hawaiian families emphasized communal caregiving. A child often has relationships with multiple caretakers, including grandparents, aunties, uncles, and other community members.  \n- A parent who tries to isolate a child from the other parent disrupts these community ties. Citing cultural values can resonate with judges who recognize that “best interests” might encompass cultural continuity and the child’s identity within a larger family network.  \n- Legal sources and commentaries from the Library of Congress on Native Hawaiian law may highlight that the court’s approach can integrate cultural considerations.  \n- While the best interest standard is the same for all families, referencing cultural contexts can underscore that alienation is not just a private issue—it’s also a tear in the social fabric and the child’s cultural inheritance.\n\n**Practical Takeaway**: Presenting the child’s best interests through a cultural lens can give the argument more depth. A family’s cultural context can reinforce the importance of maintaining open lines of contact, building on communal values that discourage false accusations and unilateral estrangement.\n\n---\n\n### Synthesis and Strategic Use of the Expanded Research\n\n1. **Statutes and Rules**:  \n   - Start with a solid, statute-based argument. Specific Fields\n\nSome fields in the API can be complicated. This page goes into greater detail about this topic.\n\nFields\n\nCase Names\n\nCase names are a complicated topic, and there are a few common misconceptions about them:\n\n\n\n\n\nCase names are not unique. There's nothing stopping a court from using Johnson v. State every time a person named Johnson sues the State. Indeed, this is common.\n\n\n\nCase names are not stable. Many cases begin their lives by suing the governor or the attorney general. But these people change as a result of elections or appointments, and so the names of these cases often change too.\n\n\n\nCase names don't always contain v. Instead, many cases start with In Re or other abbreviations.\n\nWe've done our best to normalize case names wherever we can, following Blue Book conventions. Some things we regularly do include:\n\n\n\n\n\nWe normalize all the different ways people write \"United States\" (U.S.A., United States of America, U.S., etc.) All of these variations simply become \"United States\", as the Blue Book requires.\n\n\n\nWe remove some abbreviations, like Et al.\n\n\n\nWe replace any instance of vs. with v.\n\n\n\nWe do our best to make the case names Title Case rather than UPPERCASE, as many courts publish them.\n\nThe result of all this work is that we have pretty good case names.\n\nIn the API, you'll see case names in a variety of places due to the fact that they can change over time. For example, there are case_name fields on the Docket object and also on the Opinion Cluster objects. In almost all instances, these values are the same but some cases have different values for the Docket than for an Opinion Cluster, so we keep this data in duplicate.\n\nCase names can also vary considerably in length, and we've identified three different types of case names:\n\n\n\n\n\ncase_name: This is a typical case name that can be used in almost all references. An example might be Roe v. Wade.\n\n\n\ncase_name_short: This is a shortened one or two word case name that can be used in legal writing after the standard case name has been provided by the author. An example of this might be simply Roe used, \"As was stated in Roe…\"\n\n\n\ncase_name_full: This is the full list of plaintiffs and defendants in a case, sometimes going on for hundreds of words, and often including titles or other information. For example: Roe Et Al v. Wade, District Attorney of Dallas County.\n\nAll cases have at least one of these values, many have two values, and some have all three. A case_name_short was generated algorithmically for every case possible, but about 40% of cases were too complicated for our program to process and so they were left blank. Editors have ensured that every Supreme Court case from 1945 to 2018 has a case_name_short value.\n\ncase_name is available for the majority of cases, except those that were imported from Resource.org, which only provided case_name_full values. When that happened, there was no way for us to condense a case_name_full, so until an editor is available to review them, they will lack this value. All cases have either a case_name or a case_name_full value.\n\nOur advice is to use a case_name if it is available and to fall back on the case_name_full if it is not. If you are interested in sponsoring trained humans to improve this data, please get in touch.\n\nThe absolute_url Field\n\nThe absolute_url field shows the URL where a resource can be seen live on the site. It is absolute in the sense that it should never change and will always be backwards compatible if changes are ever needed.\n\nIn some cases you might start with a URL from CourtListener, and you might want to look up the item in the API. Generally, CourtListener URLs are designed to contain an ID that can be used in the API to look it up, following a pattern like:\n\n/$type/$id/$name-of-the-case/\n\nThere are three sections:\n\n\n\n\n\n$type: This is the type of object that has been returned, for example, \"docket\" indicates that you have gotten a docket as your result.\n\n\n\n$id: This is a numeric ID for the document. This value increments as we add content to the system. Note that due to deletions and modifications the numeric IDs are not always sequential, but they will never be duplicated within a document type.\n\n\n\n$name-of-the-case: This is the \"slug\" of the document, and generally mirrors its case name. This value can change if we clean up a case name, but provided it is not omitted completely, this part of the URL can be any value without affecting the page that is loaded.\n\nPut another way, we load pages based on the $id and $type, not by the name of the case.\n\nFile Download Fields\n\nAPI responses will give you the URL path to a resource such as a PDF or MP3, but not the domain. These are often in a field named local_path or similar.\n\nTo download a resource, create a full URL by concatenating the path from the API response with https://storage.courtlistener.com/.\n\nPlease Support Open Legal Dat\n\n\n",

      "content": "It looks like you’re exploring the CourtListener API, which provides structured data about court cases, dockets, opinions, and more. The snippet you shared includes both a sample request and a response from the CourtListener REST API’s root endpoint. Here’s a detailed breakdown and how you might use this information:\n\n### What You Sent\n\n**Request:**\n```\nGET /api/rest/v4/             27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9\n\nAuthorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9\n```\n\nThis indicates a GET request to the base endpoint of the CourtListener API (`/api/rest/v4/`). The `Authorization: Token ...` header shows that you’re authenticated using a valid API token.\n\n**Example cURL Command:**\n```\ncurl \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/clusters/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9'\n```\n\nThis cURL request is similar but queries the `/clusters/` endpoint specifically. “Clusters” in CourtListener usually refer to opinion clusters—groupings of all opinions related to a single case.\n\n**Response:**\n```\nHTTP 200 OK\nContent-Type: application/json\n\n{\n    \"search\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/search/\",\n    \"dockets\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/\",\n    \"originating-court-information\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/originating-court-information/\",\n    \"docket-entries\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/docket-entries/\",\n    ...\n    \"citation-lookup\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\"\n}\n```\n\nThis JSON object is essentially a directory or roadmap of all the available endpoints at version 4 of the REST API. Each key corresponds to a type of resource you can access, and each value is the URL endpoint where you can GET that data.\n\n### What Each Endpoint Represents\n\n- **search**: Allows searching the database for cases, opinions, and more using query parameters.\n- **dockets**: Provides access to docket information for various cases. A docket is the official summary of proceedings in a court case.\n- **originating-court-information**: Contains metadata about the original (lower) courts from which a case may have originated.\n- **docket-entries**: Access the individual entries within a docket—each entry might correspond to a filing, order, or hearing.\n- **opinions, clusters, opinions-cited**: These endpoints give you access to the texts of judicial opinions, groupings of related opinions (clusters), and opinions cited by others.\n- **courts**: Information about different courts within the CourtListener database, including jurisdiction and other metadata.\n- **parties, attorneys**: Details about parties involved in cases and their attorneys.\n- **recap-related endpoints**: RECAP is a system that gathers documents from PACER. These endpoints allow access to documents and related data fetched through RECAP.\n- **tags, docket-tags**: Tools for organizing and filtering cases by tags.\n- **financial-disclosures**, **investments**, **reimbursements**, etc.: Provide financial disclosure information (often for judges or other officials).\n- **citation-lookup**: Used to find a case by its citation, making it easier if you know the citation format but not the internal ID.\n\n### How to Use These Endpoints\n\n1. **Discoverability**: The root endpoint (`/api/rest/v4/`) gives you a roadmap. If you want dockets, follow the `dockets` link. If you want opinions, follow the `opinions` link, and so forth.\n\n2. **Authentication**: You’ve already included a token in the header, which means you have access to endpoints that may require authentication. Not all endpoints need it, but many features do, such as searching large datasets or downloading certain documents.\n\n3. **Filtering and Query Parameters**: Many endpoints (like `/search/` or `/dockets/`) allow query parameters to refine results. For example, `?court=hi` might filter results to Hawai`i courts, or `?date_filed__gte=YYYY-MM-DD` might filter cases by filing date. Refer to the CourtListener documentation for available filters.\n\n4. **Pagination and Result Navigation**: Results are often paginated. Look for `next` or `previous` fields in the JSON responses to navigate through multiple pages of data.\n\n5. **Combining Data**: You can use `docket` and `docket-entries` endpoints together: first get the docket, then follow the `docket-entries` endpoint to list filings. Similarly, once you identify a cluster (a group of opinions), you can fetch individual `opinions` for the full text.\n\n### Advanced Field Details (From the Help Section)\n\n- **Case Names**: The API normalizes case names, removing inconsistent formatting and unnecessary abbreviations. You’ll see fields like `case_name`, `case_name_full`, and sometimes `case_name_short`. Use `case_name` if available, and fall back on `case_name_full` if it’s not.\n\n- **absolute_url**: This field points to a stable URL on CourtListener’s site. It’s a way to find the web-facing version of the resource. If you need to display a link to the case on a website, this is the URL you could use.\n\n- **File Downloads**: Some endpoints might provide a `local_path` for documents like PDFs. To download these, prepend `https://storage.courtlistener.com/` to the `local_path`.\n\n### Practical Use Cases\n\n- **Researching Cases**: If you’re interested in specific Hawaii family law cases, you could use `search` and filter by jurisdiction or keyword. Then use `clusters` or `opinions` to read the rulings.\n- **Building a Database**: Integrate these endpoints into your own legal research tool. Fetch dockets, parse them for procedural history, get related opinions, and store summaries in a local database.\n- **Citation Work**: Use `citation-lookup` to quickly find a case by its standard citation, making it easier to integrate with your own legal workflows.\n\n---\n\n**In Summary**:  \nThe snippet you posted is a top-level API directory from CourtListener, showing what endpoints are available and how they’re structured. By following the links and using your token, you can explore dockets, opinions, and more, then integrate that data into your legal research tools or workflows.",

Please get in touch to access this API.\n\nBack to API Docs\n\nPACER Data APIs\n\nUse these APIs to access almost half a billion items we have in our collection of PACER data.\n\nTo learn more about what's in the collection and how we gather PACER data each day, see our coverage page on the topic.\n\nThis data is organized into a number of objects. An overview of these objects is described in this section, and greater detail is provided for each, below.\n\nIn any legal proceeding, there are roughly three things: Documents, people, and organizations. Documents are grouped together into docket entries, which are grouped together into dockets. People and organizations are examples of parties. Parties have attorneys who act on their behalf in particular ways, which we call the attorney's role in the case.\n\nEach of these relationships is interlinked and has metadata that describes it. Use these APIs to explore this data.\n\nDockets, Courts, Docket Entries, and Documents\n\nA docket is a list of docket entries and some metadata. Each docket entry is a collection of documents that is uploaded to the court by a party or their attorney at a given time.\n\nThe endpoints described in this section explain these objects and how they can be accessed in our system.\n\nDockets — /api/rest/v4/dockets/\n\nDocket objects sit at the top of the object hierarchy. In our PACER database, dockets link together docket entries, parties, and attorneys.\n\nIn our case law database, dockets sit above Opinion Clusters. In our oral argument database, they sit above Audio objects.\n\nTo look up field descriptions or options for filtering, ordering, or rendering, complete an HTTP OPTIONS request:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  -X OPTIONS \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/\"\n\nTo look up a particular docket, use its ID:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/4214664/\"\n\nThe response you get will not list the docket entries, parties, or attorneys for the docket (doing so doesn't scale), but will have many other metadata fields:\n\n{\n  \"resource_uri\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/4214664/\",\n  \"id\": 4214664,\n  \"court\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/courts/dcd/\",\n  \"court_id\": \"dcd\",\n  \"original_court_info\": null,\n  \"idb_data\": null,\n  \"clusters\": [],\n  \"audio_files\": [],\n  \"assigned_to\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/people/1124/\",\n  \"referred_to\": null,\n  \"absolute_url\": \"/docket/4214664/national-veterans-legal-services-program-v-united-states/\",\n  \"date_created\": \"2016-08-20T07:25:37.448945-07:00\",\n  \"date_modified\": \"2024-05-20T03:59:23.387426-07:00\",\n  \"source\": 9,\n  \"appeal_from_str\": \"\",\n  \"assigned_to_str\": \"Paul L. Friedman\",\n  \"referred_to_str\": \"\",\n  \"panel_str\": \"\",\n  \"date_last_index\": \"2024-05-20T03:59:23.387429-07:00\",\n  \"date_cert_granted\": null,\n  \"date_cert_denied\": null,\n  \"date_argued\": null,\n  \"date_reargued\": null,\n  \"date_reargument_denied\": null,\n  \"date_filed\": \"2016-04-21\",\n  \"date_terminated\": null,\n  \"date_last_filing\": \"2024-05-15\",\n  \"case_name_short\": \"\",\n  \"case_name\": \"NATIONAL VETERANS LEGAL SERVICES PROGRAM v. United States\",\n  \"case_name_full\": \"\",\n  \"slug\": \"national-veterans-legal-services-program-v-united-states\",\n  \"docket_number\": \"1:16-cv-00745\",\n  \"docket_number_core\": \"1600745\",\n  \"pacer_case_id\": \"178502\",\n  \"cause\": \"28:1346 Tort Claim\",\n  \"nature_of_suit\": \"Other Statutory Actions\",\n  \"jury_demand\": \"None\",\n  \"jurisdiction_type\": \"U.S. Government Defendant\",\n  \"appellate_fee_status\": \"\",\n  \"appellate_case_type_information\": \"\",\n  \"mdl_status\": \"\",\n  \"filepath_ia\": \"https://www.archive.org/download/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502.docket.xml\",\n  \"filepath_ia_json\": \"https://archive.org/download/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502.docket.json\",\n  \"ia_upload_failure_count\": null,\n  \"ia_needs_upload\": true,\n  \"ia_date_first_change\": \"2018-09-30T00:00:00-07:00\",\n  \"date_blocked\": null,\n  \"blocked\": false,\n  \"appeal_from\": null,\n  \"tags\": [\n    \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/tag/1316/\"\n  ],\n  \"panel\": []\n}\n\nIdeally, docket entries, parties, and attorneys would be nested within the docket object you request, but this is not possible because some dockets have a vast number of these objects. Listing so many values in a single response from the server is impractical. To access docket entries, parties, or attorneys for a specific docket, use the docket entry, party, or attorney endpoints and filter by docket ID.\n\nThe court fields are references to our Court API, described below.\n\nCourts — /api/rest/v4/courts/\n\nThis API contains data about the courts we have in our database, and is joined into nearly every other API so that you can know where an event happened, a judge worked, etc.\n\nTo look up field descriptions or options for filtering, ordering, or rendering, complete an HTTP OPTIONS request.\n\nYou can generally cache this API. It does not change often.\n\nDocket Entries — /api/rest/v4/docket-entries/\n\nDocket Entry objects represent the rows on a PACER docket, and contain one or more nested documents. This follows the design on PACER, in which a single row on a docket represents a document with its associated attachments.\n\nTo look up field descriptions or options for filtering, ordering, or rendering, complete an HTTP OPTIONS request.\n\nTo filter to the docket entries for a particular docket use the docketfilter:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/docket-entries/?docket=4214664\"\n\nSuch a request will return up to 20 docket entries per page. Each docket entry returned can contain a number of nested documents in the recap_document key, including their full extracted text (see details in the next section below). As a result, this response can be quite large.\n\nYou can also order the results using specific fields. To order results, use the order_by query parameter. For example, to order docket entries by their filing date in ascending order:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/docket-entries/?order_by=date_filed\"\n\nTo order in descending order, prepend a - to the field name. For example, ?order_by=-date_filed will order by filing date in descending order.\n\nThe following fields can be used for ordering:\n\n\n\n\n\nid\n\n\n\ndate_created\n\n\n\ndate_modified\n\n\n\ndate_filed\n\n\n\nrecap_sequence_number\n\n\n\nentry_number\n\nTo order using multiple fields simultaneously, separate the field names with commas. For example, ?order_by=recap_sequence_number,entry_number will use the default website order for Docket Entries.\n\nA few field-level notes:\n\nFieldNotesentry_number\n\nIn district courts, this field is usually a number between zero and the low thousands (depending on the length of the case).\n\nSome appellate courts do not provide this number, in which case we use the internal PACER document ID to populate this field.\n\ndescriptionThis field contains the description of the docket entry, if we have it. A second, shorter description is also available on the document itself.recap_documentsThis field contains all the documents associated with the docket entry. In general, this is only one or two items, but it can be more in complex litigation. See below for details.recap_sequence_number\npacer_sequence_numberUse the RECAP sequence number to sort dockets in your system. It is based on the PACER sequence number when we have it, plus some heuristics to order content as accurately as possible. In rare cases, docket entry numbers are not sequential, and these fields are preferred.\n\nThis endpoint is only available to select users. Please get in touch to access this API.\n\nDocuments — /api/rest/v4/recap-documents/\n\nEach docket entry contains several documents, which we call RECAP Document objects.\n\nTo look up field descriptions or options for filtering, ordering, or rendering, complete an HTTP OPTIONS request.\n\nA few field-level notes:\n\nFieldNotesplain_text\n\nThis field contains the extracted text of the document.\n\nWe use Doctor to complete this task. If needed, Doctor uses an optimized version of Tesseract to complete OCR.\n\nTo see whether OCR was used, check the ocr_status field.\n\nfilepath_local\n\nThis field contains the path to the binary file if we have it (is_available=True). To use this field, see the help article on this topic.\n\nThe name of this field dates back to when all our files were locally stored on a single server.\n\nThis endpoint is only available to select users. Please get in touch to access this API.\n\nParties — /api/rest/v4/parties/\n\nThe Party endpoint provides details about parties that have been involved in federal cases in PACER, and contains nested attorney information.\n\nTo look up field descriptions or options for filtering, ordering, or rendering, complete an HTTP OPTIONS request.\n\nThis API can be filtered by docket ID to show all the parties for a particular case.\n\nListen Up: Filters apply to this endpoint, not the data nested within it. Therefore, each party returned by this API will list all the attorneys that have represented them in any case, even if the parties themselves are filtered to a particular case.\n\nFor example, this query returns the parties for docket number 123:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/parties/?docket=123\"\n\nIt returns something like:\n\n{\n① \"next\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/parties/42/\",\n      \"id\": 42,\n②    \"attorneys\": [\n        {\n          \"attorney\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/attorneys/1/\",\n Please get in touch to access these endpoints.\n\nOriginating Court — /api/rest/v4/originating-court-information/\n\nOriginating Court Information represents the information gathered at an appellate court about a case when it was in a lower court or administrative body.\n\nThe information in this table is joined via a one-to-one relationship to the Docket object. Generally, this table is only completed for appellate cases that we acquire from PACER.\n\nCross-walking from the upper court docket to the lower is possible using the the docket_number and appeal_from fields.\n\nIntegrated Database — /api/rest/v4/fjc-integrated-database/\n\nFJC Integrated Database objects represent the information available in the Federal Judicial Center's Integrated Database, a regularly updated source of metadata about federal court cases. You can learn more about the IDB from the following sources:\n\n\n\n\n\nThe FJC IDB Homepage\n\n\n\nOur datasheet on the IDB\n\n\n\nThe various codebooks for civil, criminal, appellate, and bankruptcy datasets.\n\nAs always, you can find our interpretations of these fields by performing an OPTIONS request on this endpoint.\n\nNote: Pending further support, this endpoint should be considered experimental quality. It is not guaranteed to have all of the available data sets, may not have the latest quarterly data, and indeed may have bugs. If you encounter any bugs, please let us know. If you would like better guarantees about the quality of this endpoint, we are enthusiastic about finding partners to better support it.\n\nFast Document Lookup — /api/rest/v4/recap-query/\n\nThis API is used to check if documents with known IDs are available in our system.\n\nTo use it, provide a court ID and a comma-separated list of pacer_doc_id's:\n\ncurl \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  'https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/recap-query/?docket_entry__docket__court=dcd&pacer_doc_id__in=04505578698,04505578717' \\\n  \n\nThis will return one entry for each document found, up to a maximum of 300 items:\n\n{\n  \"next\": null,\n  \"previous\": null,\n  \"results\": [\n    {\n      \"pacer_doc_id\": \"04505578717\",\n      \"filepath_local\": \"recap/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502.2.0_54.pdf\",\n      \"id\": 2974081\n    },\n    {\n      \"pacer_doc_id\": \"04505578698\",\n      \"filepath_local\": \"recap/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502/gov.uscourts.dcd.178502.1.0_48.pdf\",\n      \"id\": 2974077\n    }\n  ]\n}\n\nCourtListener court IDs match the subdomains on PACER, except for the following mapping:\n\nPACER CodeCL IDDescriptionazbarbArizona Bankruptcy CourtcofcuscfcCourt of Federal ClaimsnebnebraskabNebraska Bankruptcynysb-meganysbDo not use \"mega\"\n\nCareful: When placing queries, the fourth digit of a PACER document ID can be a zero or one.       "content": "Below is a structured summary and key insights from the documentation you’ve shared on the CourtListener APIs, specifically focusing on PACER data, dockets, entries, parties, and related endpoints. This is intended to help integrate these resources into legal research workflows or to understand how to fetch and analyze specific federal case information.\n\n---\n\n### Overview of Available Endpoints\n\n**Note**: Certain endpoints or data fields are only available to select users. If you encounter restricted endpoints, you’ll need to contact CourtListener for access.\n\n1. **Dockets**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/dockets/`\n   - **Data Provided**: Metadata about federal cases (dockets) including assigned judges, court details, case names, docket numbers, filing dates, and more.  \n   - **Important Points**:  \n     - Docket entries, parties, and attorneys are *not* listed directly in the docket resource (to avoid massive payloads for cases with many entries).  \n     - To get associated entries, parties, or attorneys, you must use their respective endpoints filtered by the docket ID.\n   - **Example**:  \n     ```bash\n     curl -H 'Authorization: Token YOUR_TOKEN' \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/4214664/\"\n     ```\n\n2. **Courts**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/courts/`  \n   - **Data Provided**: Court-specific metadata, including names, locations, and jurisdictions.  \n   - **Usage**: Provides context for where a case is heard and can be used to filter results or identify the correct court code.\n\n3. **Docket Entries**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/docket-entries/`  \n   - **Data Provided**: Individual docket entries representing filings, orders, and other actions taken in a case. Entries can include references to documents.  \n   - **Filtering**: Use `?docket=DOCKET_ID` to retrieve all entries for a given docket.  \n   - **Ordering and Pagination**:  \n     - Default returns up to 20 entries per page.  \n     - Use `?order_by=date_filed` or `?order_by=-date_filed` for sorting results.\n   - **Documents**: Each entry may reference documents stored and accessible through `recap_documents`.\n\n4. **Documents** (RECAP Documents):  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/recap-documents/`  \n   - **Data Provided**: Binary files (PDFs), OCR’ed text, metadata about how the document was acquired.  \n   - **Usage**: After identifying docket entries and their associated documents, you can use `recap_documents` to fetch the actual text or PDF.  \n   - **Access Restrictions**: Often restricted; requires special permission.\n\n5. **Parties**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/parties/`  \n   - **Data Provided**: Information about parties involved in a case.  \n   - **Filtering**: `?docket=DOCKET_ID` returns parties for that docket. However, the attorneys nested under a party may include representation in multiple dockets, not just the filtered one.  \n   - **Party Types**: Indicates roles like Plaintiff, Defendant, Trustee, etc. In criminal cases, can include offense details.\n\n6. **Attorneys**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/attorneys/`  \n   - **Data Provided**: Information about attorneys, their contact info, and which parties they represent in which cases.  \n   - **Filtering**: `?docket=DOCKET_ID` to see attorneys related to that docket. Similar to parties, the association with parties may not be filtered to that single docket.\n\n7. **Originating Court Information**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/originating-court-information/`  \n   - **Data Provided**: Links an appellate case to the lower court information. Useful for appellate cases where you need to trace back the origin.\n\n8. **FJC Integrated Database**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/fjc-integrated-database/`  \n   - **Data Provided**: Data from the Federal Judicial Center’s integrated database. Contains structured metadata about federal cases.  \n   - **Quality and Completeness**: Considered experimental. Not guaranteed complete or bug-free.\n\n9. **Fast Document Lookup (RECAP Query)**:  \n   - **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/recap-query/`  \n   - **Usage**: Quickly check if documents with known PACER IDs exist in CourtListener’s system.  \n   - **Filtering by Court and Document ID**: `?docket_entry__docket__court=[court_id]&pacer_doc_id__in=[doc_ids]`\n   - **Normalization**: Watch out for zero vs. one in the 4th digit of `pacer_doc_id`.\n\n---\n\n### Use Cases in Research\n\n- **Identifying Case History**:  \n  Start with `/dockets/` to find a case by ID. Then get the docket’s metadata. Once you have a docket ID, you can fetch all filings (`/docket-entries/?docket=ID`) to understand the procedural history.\n\n- **Retrieving Documents**:  \n  After identifying the relevant docket entries and their `recap_documents`, you can fetch PDFs or text versions of the filings. This helps in reading original motions, orders, and judgments.\n\n- **Attorney and Party Analysis**:  \n  Use `/parties/` and `/attorneys/` to see who represented whom, check for conflicts of interest, or evaluate attorney activity across multiple dockets.\n\n- **Court and Jurisdiction Context**:  \n  Look up `/courts/` for metadata on the court handling the case. This is helpful for understanding the procedural posture and local rules or precedents.\n\n- **Historical and Statistical Research**:  \n  Integrate the FJC Integrated Database for broader statistical analysis of case trends, durations, and outcomes across multiple courts and case types.\n\n- **Appellate Review**:  \n  For appellate cases, the `originating-court-information` endpoint can reveal the lower court’s docket number and details, allowing you to trace the litigation path from trial to appellate level.\n\n---\n\n### Authentication and Access\n\n- **API Token**:  \n  All requests shown include an `Authorization: Token YOUR_TOKEN` header. Make sure you have the correct token and the necessary permissions.\n\n- **Selective Availability**:  \n  Some endpoints or data fields are only available to select users. If you’re encountering restricted resources, consider reaching out to CourtListener for elevated access.\n\n---\n\n### Notes and Tips\n\n- **Pagination**: Many endpoints return large volumes of data. Pay attention to the `next` and `previous` fields in responses for pagination.\n- **Filtering & Ordering**: Use query parameters like `?docket=ID` or `?order_by=` fields to tailor responses. This reduces response size and complexity.\n- **Caching and Performance**: Court data can be stable. Some endpoints like `/courts/` don’t change often and can be cached locally.\n- **Case Names & IDs**: CourtListener normalizes case names and provides multiple forms (`case_name`, `case_name_full`, `case_name_short`). Use `case_name` by default and fallback to `case_name_full` if needed.\n\n---\n\n**In Summary**:  \nThese APIs provide a comprehensive ecosystem to access structured legal data from federal dockets, related documents, parties, attorneys, and more. By chaining endpoints together (e.g., from dockets to docket entries to documents), you can reconstruct a full procedural history and gather primary source materials for legal research.",

      "content": "Financial Disclosures API\n\nFinancial Disclosures API\n\nUse these APIs to work with financial disclosure records of current and former federal judges.\n\nThis data was collected from senate records and information requests we sent to the federal judiciary. You can learn more about which disclosures are included and the limitations of these APIs on our coverage page for financial disclosures.\n\nJudicial officers and certain judicial employees in the United States are required to file financial disclosure reports by Title I of the Ethics in Government Act of 1978. The Act requires that designated federal officials publicly disclose their personal financial interests to ensure confidence in the integrity of the federal government by demonstrating that they are able to carry out their duties without compromising the public trust.\n\nThese APIs were used by the Wall Street Journal in their 17-part exposé about the hidden conflicts of federal judges. That led to Congress passing the Courthouse Ethics and Transparency Act to put this information online. It was also used by ProPublica in their Pulitzer prize winning reporting about failures to disclose gifts and perks.\n\nThis data is updated in partnership with organizations using it. Please get in touch if you would like to work together to process and ingest the latest disclosure records.\n\nAvailable APIs\n\nThe Ethics in Government Act details the types of information required, and prescribes the general format and procedures for the reports themselves.\n\nThe APIs described below mirror the Act's language, with APIs corresponding to each required disclosure type.\n\nDisclosures — /api/rest/v4/financial-disclosures/\n\nThis API contains information about the main document itself and is the link between the other financial disclosure endpoints and the judges in our system.\n\nInvestments — /api/rest/v4/investments/\n\nThis API lists the source and type of investment income held by a judge, including dividends, rents, interest, capital gains, or income from qualified or excepted trusts.\n\nPositions — /api/rest/v4/disclosure-positions/\n\nThis API lists the positions held as an officer, director, trustee, general partner, proprietor, representative, executor, employee, or consultant of any corporation, company, firm, partnership, trust, or other business enterprise, any nonprofit organization, any labor organization, or any educational or other institution other than the United States.\n\nAgreements — /api/rest/v4/agreements/\n\nThis API lists any agreements or arrangements of the filer in existence at any time during the reporting period.\n\nNon-Investment Income\n/api/rest/v4/non-investment-incomes/\n\nThis API lists the source, type, and the amount or value of earned or other non-investment income aggregating $200 or more from any one source that is received during the reporting period.\n\nNon-Investment Income (Spouse)\n/api/rest/v4/spouse-incomes/\n\nThis API lists the source and type earned of non-investment income from the spouse of the filer.\n\nReimbursements — /api/rest/v4/reimbursements/\n\nThis API lists the source identity and description (including travel locations, dates, and nature of expenses provided) of any travel-related reimbursements aggregating more than $415 in value that are received by the filer from one source during the reporting period.\n\nGifts — /api/rest/v4/gifts/\n\nThis API lists the source, a brief description, and the value of all gifts aggregating more than $415 in value that are received by the filer during the reporting period from any one source.\n\nDebts — /api/rest/v4/debts/\n\nAll liabilities specified by that section that are owed during the period beginning on January 1 of the preceding calendar year and ending fewer than 31 days before the date on which the report is filed.\n\nFields\n\nUnderstanding the Fields\n\nLike most of our APIs, field definitions can be obtained by sending an HTTP OPTIONS request to any of the APIs. For example, this request, piped through jq, shows you the fields of the Gifts API:\n\ncurl -X OPTIONS \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/gifts/\" \\\n    | jq '.actions.POST'\n\n{\n  \"resource_uri\": {\n    \"type\": \"field\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": true,\n    \"label\": \"Resource uri\"\n  },\n  \"id\": {\n    \"type\": \"field\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": true,\n    \"label\": \"Id\"\n  },\n  \"date_created\": {\n    \"type\": \"datetime\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": true,\n    \"label\": \"Date created\",\n    \"help_text\": \"The moment when the item was created.\"\n  },\n  \"date_modified\": {\n    \"type\": \"datetime\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": true,\n    \"label\": \"Date modified\",\n    \"help_text\": \"The last moment when the item was modified. A value in year 1750 indicates the value is unknown\"\n  },\n  \"source\": {\n    \"type\": \"string\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": false,\n    \"label\": \"Source\",\n    \"help_text\": \"Source of the judicial gift. (ex. Alta Ski Area).\"\n  },\n  \"description\": {\n    \"type\": \"string\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": false,\n    \"label\": \"Description\",\n    \"help_text\": \"Description of the gift (ex. Season Pass).\"\n  },\n  \"value\": {\n    \"type\": \"string\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": false,\n    \"label\": \"Value\",\n    \"help_text\": \"Value of the judicial gift, (ex. $1,199.00)\"\n  },\n  \"redacted\": {\n    \"type\": \"boolean\",\n    \"required\": false,\n    \"read_only\": false,\n    \"label\": \"Redacted\",\n    \"help_text\": \"Does the gift row contain redaction(s)?\"\n  },\n  \"financial_disclosure\": {\n    \"type\": \"field\",\n    \"required\": true,\n    \"read_only\": false,\n    \"label\": \"Financial disclosure\",\n    \"help_text\": \"The financial disclosure associated with this gift.\"\n  }\n}\n\nNote that each field has the following attributes:\n\n\n\n\n\ntype: Indicating the object type for the field.\n\n\n\nrequired: Indicating whether the field can have null values. Note that string fields will be blank instead of null.\n\n\n\nread_only: Indicates whether the field can be updated by users (this does not apply to read-only APIs like the financial disclosure APIs).\n\n\n\nlabel: This is a human-readable form for the field's name.\n\n\n\nhelp_text: This explains the meaning of the field.\n\nRedactions\n\nFor security reasons, filers can redact information on their disclosure forms. When a line in a disclosure contains a redaction, we will attempt to set the redacted field on that row to True. This is your hint that you may want to investigate that row more carefully.\n\nThis field can be used as a filter. For example, here are all the investments with redacted information:\n\ncurl \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/investments/?redacted=True\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9'\n{\n  \"next\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/investments/?page=2&redacted=True&cursor=cD0xMjA5NjAyMg%3D%3D\",\n  \"previous\": null,\n  \"results\": [\n    {\n      \"resource_uri\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/investments/5385644/\",\n      \"id\": 5385644,\n      \"date_created\": \"2023-04-17T11:03:22.404170-07:00\",\n      \"date_modified\": \"2023-04-17T11:03:22.404185-07:00\",\n      \"page_number\": 4,\n      \"description\": \"Common Stock\",\n      \"redacted\": true,\n      \"income_during_reporting_period_code\": \"G\",\n      \"income_during_reporting_period_type\": \"Dividend\",\n      \"gross_value_code\": \"P2\",\n      \"gross_value_method\": \"T\",\n      \"transaction_during_reporting_period\": \"\",\n      \"transaction_date_raw\": \"\",\n      \"transaction_date\": null,\n      \"transaction_value_code\": \"\",\n      \"transaction_gain_code\": \"\",\n      \"transaction_partner\": \"\",\n      \"has_inferred_values\": false,\n      \"financial_disclosure\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/financial-disclosures/34187/\"\n    },\n...\n\nValue Codes\n\nSeveral APIs, including Investments, Debts,and Gifts use form-based value codes to indicate monetary ranges instead of exact values. For example, the letter \"J\" indicates a value of $1–15,000.\n\nPlace an OPTIONS request to these endpoints to learn the values of those fields or look in a PDF filing to see the key.\n\nRegrettably, these fields have not been updated by the judiciary in many years, so the highest value code only goes up to $50,000,000. For some judges, this may not be enough to accurately reflect their wealth.\n\nInferred Values\n\nInvestment objects contain the field has_inferred_values. This field indicates that we inferred information about an investment based on the layout of the data in the disclosure form.\n\nFor example, an investment could have been bought in Q1, while a dividend was paid out in Q2 before being sold in Q4. Often, after the first entry of the investment, later rows in the table are mostly blank. In this instance, we infer the values.\n\nThe table below gives a brief example where we would infer that the blank cell below the cell for AAPL also refers to AAPL:\n\nDescriptionDateTypeAAPL2020-01-01Bought—2020-02-01Sold\n\nIn this (slightly contrived) example our database would have two rows in the Investment table. The first would be for the purchase of the AAPL stock, and the second would be for the sale of it.\n\nAPI Examples\n\nYou can query for investments by stock name, transaction dates and even gross values. For example, the following query is for financial disclosures with individual investments valued above $50,000,000.00. Note that this uses a value code as explained in the general notes above:\n\ncurl \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/investments/?gross_value_code=P4&fields=investments\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9'\n\nAdditionally, you could pinpoint gifts of individual judges when combining the gift database with our judicial database. The following query returns all reported gifts by the late Ruth Bader Ginsburg (her ID is 1213):\n\ncurl \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/financial-disclosures/?person=1213&fields=gifts\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9'\n\nIn 2024, we presented these APIs at the NICAR conference and created many more examples you can explore.\n\nLearn More\n\nThe following references may help you learn more about these forms:\n\n\n\n\n\nThe official policies guiding financial disclosures\n\n\n\nThe filing instructions given to judges and judicial employees\n\n\n\nA GAO report on disclosures\n\n\n\nThe Ethics in Government Act establishing disclosure rules\n\nSecurity\n\nPlease report any security or privacy concerns to security@free.law.\n\nPlease Support Open Legal Data\n\nThese services are sponsored by Free Law Project and users like you.       "content": "Below is a structured overview and key points drawn from the Financial Disclosures API documentation you provided. This information is intended to help understand how to access, interpret, and utilize financial disclosure data available through the CourtListener APIs. \n\n---\n\n### Purpose and Context\n\nFederal judges must file financial disclosures under the Ethics in Government Act of 1978 to promote transparency and public trust. These filings may include investments, positions, agreements, income, reimbursements, gifts, and debts. The CourtListener Financial Disclosures API allows users (with the appropriate permissions) to access and analyze these records.\n\nThese data points have been critical in investigative journalism, legislative changes, and academic research. They supported efforts like the Wall Street Journal’s exposé on judicial conflicts of interest and ProPublica’s Pulitzer Prize-winning reporting, ultimately influencing legislation such as the Courthouse Ethics and Transparency Act.\n\n### Available Endpoints\n\nEach endpoint corresponds to a type of financial disclosure data required by the Ethics in Government Act. All endpoints support OPTIONS requests to retrieve field definitions, valid filters, and allowable query parameters.\n\n1. **Financial Disclosures**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/financial-disclosures/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Metadata about the disclosure filings themselves. This is the central link to data in other endpoints.  \n   **Use Case**: Identify which disclosures belong to which judges, or filter by judge ID (`person`) to see disclosures associated with a particular official.\n\n2. **Investments**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/investments/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Information on the judge’s investment income (e.g., stocks, bonds, trusts), dividends, interests, rents, capital gains, and their value.  \n   **Value Codes**: Instead of exact amounts, judges often use value codes indicating ranges. Example: `J` might mean $1–15,000.  \n   **Inferred Values**: Some data may be inferred from context, indicating that not all fields are explicitly stated on the form.  \n   **Redactions**: The `redacted` field indicates if the judge redacted part of the line item.\n\n3. **Positions**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/disclosure-positions/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Positions held by the filer (judge) in any organization (corporations, nonprofits, etc.) during the reporting period.  \n   **Use Case**: Check for potential conflicts of interest based on outside roles.\n\n4. **Agreements**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/agreements/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Any agreement or arrangement the filer was part of, which might include employment agreements, future compensation arrangements, etc.\n\n5. **Non-Investment Income**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/non-investment-incomes/` and `/api/rest/v4/spouse-incomes/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Any earned or other non-investment income over a threshold amount. Separate endpoint for spouse income.  \n   **Use Case**: Determine other income streams that might influence a judge’s decision-making or create conflicts.\n\n6. **Reimbursements**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/reimbursements/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Travel-related reimbursements exceeding a certain dollar amount, detailing source, reason, and nature of expense.  \n   **Use Case**: Identify potential influence through travel sponsorship or large reimbursements from interested entities.\n\n7. **Gifts**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/gifts/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Lists gifts valued over a certain threshold. Includes source, description, and value.  \n   **Redactions**: Check the `redacted` field.  \n   **Use Case**: Highlight possible undue influence through expensive gifts.\n\n8. **Debts**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/debts/`  \n   **What It Provides**: Liabilities exceeding certain amounts.  \n   **Use Case**: Investigate financial pressures or conflicts stemming from large debts.\n\n### Common Field Attributes\n\n- **resource_uri**, **id**: Identifiers for the record.\n- **date_created**, **date_modified**: Timestamps for record creation and updates.\n- **redacted**: Boolean indicating if the record has redacted information.\n- **help_text**: Provides clarity on the meaning of each field (available via OPTIONS requests).\n- **value codes**: Investments and some other fields use coded ranges for monetary values. Exact amounts may not be present, but you can retrieve code definitions via OPTIONS or find them in filing instructions.\n\n### Redactions and Data Gaps\n\nCertain sensitive details can be redacted by filers. The `redacted` field signals that information is missing. You might choose to investigate further or note that the data is incomplete.\n\n### Querying and Filtering\n\n- **Filtering by Person (Judge)**: For example, `?person=1213` can fetch all financial disclosures related to a specific judge with ID 1213.\n- **Filtering by Redaction**: `?redacted=True` returns all items with redactions.\n- **Filtering by Value Codes**: Filter investments by their value code to find assets above a certain threshold (e.g., `?gross_value_code=P4` might indicate very high-value investments).\n- **Chaining Queries**: Combine financial disclosures with judicial data to get a holistic view of a judge’s financial interests.\n\n### Security and Ethics\n\n- **Report Concerns**: If you find anomalies or have security concerns, report them to `security@free.law`.\n- **Public Benefit**: Data is provided by the non-profit Free Law Project. Users are encouraged to support the initiative financially or through data contributions.\n\n### Additional Resources\n\n- **Ethics in Government Act**: Establishes the legal framework for these disclosures.\n- **Filing Instructions for Judges**: Guides on how judges must complete these forms.\n- **GAO Reports & Official Policies**: Provide context and depth to the regulations governing judicial disclosures.\n\n### Supporting Open Legal Data\n\nThe Free Law Project runs CourtListener and these APIs. They rely on donations, memberships, and partner collaborations to maintain and improve the dataset. Consider contributing if these resources are valuable to your work.\n\n---\n\n**In Summary**:  \nThe Financial Disclosures API provides a transparent, structured look at the financial interests of federal judges. By examining investments, positions, agreements, income, reimbursements, gifts, and debts, researchers, journalists, and the public can assess potential conflicts of interest. The API’s structured approach, combined with filters and codes, allows users to tailor their queries, while attention to redactions and inferred values ensures a cautious and informed interpretation of the data.",

      "content": "Oral Argument Recordings APIs\n\nUse these APIs to gather and analyze the largest collection of oral argument recordings on the Internet.\n\nThe APIs\n\nOral Argument Recordings — /api/rest/v4/audio/\n\nUse this API to gather data about oral argument recordings. This API is linked to the docket API (below), which contains data about each case. It is also linked to the judge API, which has information about the judges in the case.\n\nThe audio files we gather from court websites come in many formats. After we gather the files, we convert them into optimized MP3s that have a 22050Hz sample rate and 48k bitrate. After converting the files, we set the ID3 tags to better values that we scraped. Finally, we set the cover art for the MP3 to the seal of the court, and set the publisher album art to our logo.\n\nThe original audio files can be downloaded from the court using the download_url field. If you prefer to download our enhanced version, that location is in the local_path_mp3 field. To download the file, see our help article on this topic.\n\nThe duration field contains an estimated length of the audio file, in seconds. Because these MP3s are variable bitrate, this field is based on sampling the file and is not always accurate.\n\nAs with all other APIs, you can look up the field descriptions, filtering, ordering, and rendering options by making an OPTIONS request:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  -X OPTIONS \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/audio/\"\n\nDockets — /api/rest/v4/dockets/\n\nDocket objects sit at the top of the object hierarchy. In our PACER database, dockets link together docket entries, parties, and attorneys.\n\nIn our case law database, dockets sit above Opinion Clusters. In our oral argument database, they sit above Audio objects.\n\nTo look up field descriptions or options for filtering, ordering, or rendering, complete an HTTP OPTIONS request:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  -X OPTIONS \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/\"\n\nTo look up a particular docket, use its ID:\n\ncurl -v \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/4214664/\"\n\nThe response you get will not list the docket entries, parties, or attorneys for the docket (doing so doesn't scale), but will have many other metadata fields:\n\n{\n  \"resource_uri\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/dockets/4214664/\",\n  \"id\": 4214664,\n  \"court\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/courts/dcd/\",\n  \"court_id\": \"dcd\",\n  \"original_court_info\": null,\n  \"idb_data\": null,\n  \"clusters\": [],\n  \"audio_files\": [],\n  \"assigned_to\": \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/people/1124/\",\n  \"referred_to\": null,\n  \"absolute_url\": \"/docket/4214664/national-veterans-legal-services-program-v-united-states/\",\n  \"date_created\": \"2016-08-20T07:25:37.448945-07:00\",\n  \"date_modified\": \"2024-05-20T03:59:23.387426-07:00\",\n  \"source\": 9,\n  \"appeal_from_str\": \"\",\n  \"assigned_to_str\": \"Paul L.       "content": "Below is a structured overview and key points from the documentation you provided about the Oral Argument Recordings API on CourtListener. This aims to help understand how to access oral argument audio data, integrate it with docket information, and leverage it for research or analysis.\n\n---\n\n### Purpose and Context\n\nThe Oral Argument Recordings API is designed to give users access to one of the largest public repositories of oral argument audio for court cases. By linking this audio data to dockets and related metadata, researchers, journalists, legal professionals, and the public can study courtroom proceedings in depth.\n\n### Key Endpoints\n\n1. **Oral Argument Recordings**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/audio/`  \n   **Data Provided**:  \n   - Metadata about audio files of oral arguments.\n   - Each audio record may include links to corresponding dockets or judges associated with the case.\n   - Conversion details: Original audio is converted into optimized MP3s (22050Hz, 48k bitrate) with standardized ID3 tags and cover art.\n\n   **Fields to Note**:  \n   - `download_url`: Direct link to the original audio from the court’s website.  \n   - `local_path_mp3`: A path for downloading the enhanced MP3 version. Combine this with the recommended storage domain according to the documentation.  \n   - `duration`: Estimated length of the recording in seconds. Note that this is approximate due to variable bitrates.\n\n   **OPTIONS Request**:  \n   Sending an OPTIONS request to the `/audio/` endpoint provides details on all available fields, filter options, and how to order or paginate results.\n\n2. **Dockets**:  \n   **Endpoint**: `/api/rest/v4/dockets/`  \n   **Relationship to Audio**:  \n   - Dockets serve as a hierarchical parent. In the oral argument database, each docket can have zero or more associated audio files (oral arguments).\n   - Dockets also link to case information, parties, attorneys, and possibly to opinion clusters.\n\n   **Data Provided**:  \n   - Metadata about the case, such as the court ID, assigned judges, case names, docket numbers, filing dates, and more.\n   - `audio_files`: A list (or reference) to associated audio files. Note that this may just be references, not the full audio data itself.\n\n   **OPTIONS Request**:  \n   Sending an OPTIONS request to `/dockets/` provides details on fields like `court`, `assigned_to`, `case_name`, `docket_number`, filtering, and sorting options.\n\n### Data Retrieval Flow\n\n1. **Identify a Case or Docket**:  \n   - Start by querying `/api/rest/v4/dockets/` using filters or known docket IDs.  \n   - Once you find the docket of interest, note the `id` or other identifying fields.\n\n2. **Fetch Related Audio**:  \n   - Use the `/api/rest/v4/audio/` endpoint and filter by docket or other known attributes to retrieve audio recordings of oral arguments associated with that docket.  \n   - Inspect fields like `local_path_mp3` or `download_url` to access the actual audio file.\n\n3. **Analyze and Store Data**:  \n   - Download the enhanced MP3 for offline analysis or transcription.\n   - Use the date, court, and docket metadata to organize and contextualize the audio files for research projects, presentations, or archival purposes.\n\n### Practical Applications\n\n- **Legal Research and Education**:  \n  Hear how cases are argued in court and link that understanding to the final opinions and rulings.\n  \n- **Journalism and Reporting**:  \n  Listen to oral arguments to gain insights into judicial reasoning, attorney performance, or the dynamics of particular courts.\n  \n- **Data Analysis**:  \n  Combine oral argument metadata with docket data to perform large-scale analyses—e.g., studying speech patterns, length of arguments, and trends over time.\n\n### Notes and Considerations\n\n- **Data Formats**:  \n  Audio is provided in standardized MP3 formats after conversion, making it easier to handle across various audio analysis tools.\n  \n- **Pagination and Large Results**:  \n  For cases with numerous recordings, the API may require pagination. Use `next` and `previous` fields in responses to navigate through large result sets.\n  \n- **Linking with Other CourtListener Endpoints**:  \n  Oral arguments can be combined with data from the case law (opinions), party information, and attorney endpoints for comprehensive case studies.\n\n### Support and Additional Resources\n\n- **Authentication**:  \n  As with other CourtListener APIs, you will need a valid token if required.  \n- **OPTIONS Requests for Field Definitions**:  \n  An OPTIONS request to an endpoint returns a schema of fields, filters, and allowed operations, helping tailor queries effectively.\n  \n- **Support and Donations**:  \n  CourtListener is maintained by the Free Law Project, a non-profit. Consider supporting them by donating or becoming a member, ensuring these services and data remain available and expand over time.\n\n---\n\n**In Summary**:  \nThe Oral Argument Recordings API grants access to a rich trove of audio data, linking it to case dockets and other legal information. With these tools, users can deepen their understanding of judicial processes, enhance legal research, and foster greater transparency in the legal system.",

      "content": "Citation Lookup and Verification API\n\n/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\n\nUse this API to look up citations in CourtListener's database of 17,773,085 citations.\n\nThis API can look up either an individual citation or can parse and look up every citation in a block of text. This can be useful as a guardrail to help prevent hallucinated citations.\n\nThis API uses Eyecite, a tool we developed with Harvard Library Innovation Lab to parse legal citations. To develop Eyecite, we analyzed more than 50 million citations going back more than two centuries. We believe we have identified every reporter abbreviation in American case law and that there is no case law citation that Eyecite cannot properly parse and interpret.\n\nThis API uses the same authentication and serialization methods as the rest of the CourtListener APIs. It does not support filtering, pagination, ordering, or field selection.\n\nUsage\n\nThe simplest way to query this API is to send it a blob of text. If the text does not have any citations, it will simply return an empty JSON object:\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'text=Put some text here'\\\n[]\n\nIf the text contains valid citations, it will return a list of the citations, analyzing each. This example contains a single citation that is found:\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'text=Obergefell v. Hodges (576 U.S. 644) established the right to marriage among same-sex couples'\n[\n  {\n    \"citation\": \"576 U.S. 644\",\n    \"normalized_citations\": [\n      \"576 U.S. 644\"\n    ],\n    \"start_index\": 22,\n    \"end_index\": 34,\n    \"status\": 200,\n    \"error_message\": \"\",\n    \"clusters\": [...one large cluster object here...]\n  }\n]\n\nIf you have the volume, reporter, and page for a citation, you can look it up as follows:\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'volume=576' \\\n  --data 'reporter=U.S.' \\\n  --data 'page=644'\n\nThat returns the same response as above.\n\nField Definitions\n\nThe fields returned by this API are:\n\n\n\n\n\ncitation — The citation you looked up. If you supplied the volume, reporter, and page, they will appear here as a single space-separated string.\n\n\n\nnormalized_citations — Normalized versions of your citation if it contains a typo or if it is not the canonical (standard) abbreviation for a reporter. If the citation queried is ambiguous, more than one item can appear in this field. See examples below.\n\n\n\nstart_index & end_index — These fields indicate the start and end positions where a citation is found in the text queried.\n\n\n\nstatus — indicates the outcome of a citation lookup. Its values correspond to HTTP status codes and can have one of five values:\n\n\n\n\n\n200 (OK) — We found a citation, it was valid, and we were able to look it up in CourtListener.\n\n\n\n404 (Not Found) — We found a citation, it was valid, but we were unable to look it up in CourtListener.\n\n\n\n400 (Bad Request) — We found something that looks like a citation, but the reporter in the citation wasn’t in our system (e.g., “33 Umbrella 422” looks like a citation, but is not valid).\n\n\n\n300 (Multiple Choices) — We found a valid citation, it was valid, but it matched more than one item in CourtListener.\n\n\n\n429 (Too Many Requests) — This API will only lookup 250 citations in a single request. Any citations after that point will have this status. They will be identified but will not be looked up. (See throttles below)\n\n\n\nerror_message — This field will contain additional details about any problems the lookup encounters.\n\n\n\nclusters — This is a list of the CourtListener cluster objects that match the citation in your query. This key will contain multiple values when a citation matches more than one legal decision. This can happen when a citation is ambiguous or when multiple decisions are on a single page in a printed book (and thus share the same citation).\n\nLimitations & Throttles\n\nThis API has four limitations on how much it can be used:\n\n\n\n\n\nThe performance of this API is affected by the number of citations it has to look up. Therefore, it is throttled to 60 valid citations per minute. If you are below this throttle, you will be able to send a request to the API. If a request pushes you beyond this throttle, further requests will be denied. When your request is denied, the API will respond with a 429 HTTP code and a JSON object. The JSON object will contain a wait_util key that uses an ISO-8601 datetime to indicate when you will be able to make your next request.\n\n\n\nThe API will look up at most 250 citations in any single request. Any citations past that point will be parsed, but not matched to the CourtListener database. The status key of such citations will be 429, indicating “Too many citations requested.” See examples below for details.\n\n\n\nText lookup requests to this API can only contain 64,000 characters at a time. Requests with more than this amount will be blocked for security. This is about 50 pages of legal content.\n\n\n\nTo prevent denial of service attacks that do not contain any citations, this API has the same request throttle rates as the other CourtListener APIs. This way, even requests that do not contain citations can be throttled. (Most users will never encounter this throttle.)\n\nA few other limitations to be aware of include:\n\n\n\n\n\nThis API does not look up statutes, law journals, id, or supra citations. If you wish to match such citations, please use Eyecite directly.\n\n\n\nThis API will not attempt to match citations without volume numbers or page numbers (e.g. 22 U.S. ___).\n\nAPI Examples\n\nBasic, Valid Lookup\n\nThe following is a basic lookup using the text parameter and a block of text:\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'text=Obergefell v. Hodges (576 U.S. 644) established the right to marriage among same-sex couples'\n[\n  {\n    \"citation\": \"576 U.S. 644\",\n    \"normalized_citations\": [\n      \"576 U.S. 644\"\n    ],\n    \"start_index\": 22,\n    \"end_index\": 34,\n    \"status\": 200,\n    \"error_message\": \"\",\n    \"clusters\": [...one cluster here...]\n  }\n]\n\nFailed Lookup\n\nThis query uses the volume-reporter-page triad, but fails because the citation does not exist:\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'volume=1' \\\n  --data 'reporter=U.S.' \\\n  --data 'page=200'\n[\n  {\n    \"citation\": \"1 U.S. 200\",\n    \"normalized_citations\": [\n      \"1 U.S. 200\"\n    ],\n    \"start_index\": 0,\n    \"end_index\": 10,\n    \"status\": 404,\n    \"error_message\": \"Citation not found: '1 U.S. 200'\",\n    \"clusters\": []\n  }\n]\n\nNote that:\n\n\n\n\n\nThe status field is set to 404 indicating the citation was not found.\n\n\n\nThe start_index is 0, and the end_index is the length of the citation including space separators.\n\n\n\nThe error_message field provides details of the error.\n\nThrottled Citations\n\nIf your request contains more than 250 citations, the 251st and subsequent citations will be returned with 429 status fields:\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'text=Imagine a very long blob here, with 251 citations.'\n[\n  ...250 citations would appear here, then the 251st and subsequent citations would be...\n  {\n    \"citation\": \"576 U.S. 644\",\n    \"normalized_citations\": [\n      \"576 U.S. 644\"\n    ],\n    \"start_index\": 10002,\n    \"end_index\": 10013,\n    \"status\": 429,\n    \"error_message\": \"Too many citations requested.\",\n    \"clusters\": []\n  }\n]\n\nNote that:\n\n\n\n\n\nAll citations will be parsed and will provide normalized versions and index locations.\n\n\n\nCitations after the 250th will return a status of 429, indicating \"Too many citations requested.\"\n\n\n\nA follow-up query that begins on the 251st start_index (in this case number 10002) will look up the next 250 items.\n\nTypoed/Non-Canonical Reporter Abbreviation\n\nIf you query the non-canonical reporter abbreviation or if your reporter contains a known typo, we will provide the corrected citation in the normalized_citations key. The following example looks up a citation using \"US\" instead of the correct \"U.S.\":\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'text=576 US 644'\n[\n  {\n    \"citation\": \"576 US 644\",\n    \"normalized_citations\": [\n      \"576 U.S. 644\"\n    ],\n    \"start_index\": 1,\n    \"end_index\": 11,\n    \"status\": 200,\n    \"error_message\": \"\",\n    \"clusters\": [...one cluster here...]\n  }\n]\n\nAmbiguous Citation\n\nThis lookup is for an ambiguous citation abbreviated as \"H.\" This reporter abbreviation can refer to Handy's Ohio Reports, the Hawaii Reports, or Hill’s New York Reports. Only two of those reporter series have cases at the queried volume and page number, so the API returns two possible matches for the citation:\n\ncurl -X POST \"https://www.courtlistener.com/api/rest/v4/citation-lookup/\" \\\n  --header 'Authorization: Token 27cb3521fc97253116933795c20d3987b11865e9' \\\n  --data 'text=1 H. 150'\n[\n  {\n    \"citation\": \"1 H. 150\",\n    \"normalized_citations\": [\n      \"1 Handy 150\",\n      \"1 Haw. 150\",\n      \"1 Hill 150\"\n    ],\n    \"start_index\": 0,\n    \"end_index\": 8,\n    \"status\": 300,\n    \"clusters\": [\n      {\n        ...\n        \"citations\": [{\n          \"volume\": 1,\n          \"reporter\": \"Handy\",\n          \"page\": \"150\",\n          \"type\": 2\n        }],\n       ...\n       \"case_name\": \"Louis v.
